2183 : AbhW 52.4 |AbhW 52.4: nāgeri waitālika milw amurṣita. There seems to be a connection with Pers. and Hind. nagarah, naghāreh, kettledrum (see Persian-English Dictionary s.v. naghâreh). Wilk. s.v. nĕgara III: in India the nagarah is a small drum beaten by public criers. Does the e in nageri point to a part. pronunciation of the long ā? In RY 26.23 (also 23.71?) nageri is the instrument (kettledrum); in the other passages nageri or nagerika is the person (public crier) or an adjective belonging to waitālika, etc. (beating the kettledrum).  nageri, nagerika, nageriki

2677 : AbhW 63.13 |AbhW 63.13: ... ikaṅ wwaṅ prasama masö / makamukha para taṇḍa swastya prārtha (one short syllable lacking) sakura. Kurasa and kura could perhaps be the part of a plant (root? stem?), and then sakurasa (sakura): ``of the same kurasa (kura)'', used for a relationship. Bal. com. uses sakura (bawa) to render sanak dharma (adopted child?) in RL 7.157: kaṅkĕn sanak darmâji (bal. com.: inaku sakurabawa (?) olih saṅ prabu; see KBW s.v. sakura).  kurasa II kura
